<span id="freeTextContainer15301806805597636279">I can still smell this novel; the sweat, the onions, the rayon dresses that must be burned because a certain man looked at you the wrong way, touched you the wrong way. Aliide Truu is an older woman living alone in her house in the Estonian countryside. One morning she notices a mound in her garden. A mound with blonde hair. A mound that, once Aliide decides to go outside and have a look, is wearing expensive stockings and is missing a slipper. Through a series of flashbacks we get to know the s</span>
  <span id="freeText15301806805597636279" style="display:none">I can still smell this novel; the sweat, the onions, the rayon dresses that must be burned because a certain man looked at you the wrong way, touched you the wrong way. Aliide Truu is an older woman living alone in her house in the Estonian countryside. One morning she notices a mound in her garden. A mound with blonde hair. A mound that, once Aliide decides to go outside and have a look, is wearing expensive stockings and is missing a slipper. Through a series of flashbacks we get to know the stories of Aliide and the mound, who turns out to be Zara, a young Russian girl who's trying to escape the men who've trafficked her to the West. Packed with guilt, power, shame and self-preservation, this is one of the most compelling stories I've read in a long time.</span>

<div id="review_2190982910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2190982910" />
    <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship"><img alt="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325201543p2/5229326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2190982910?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship">Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780802170774" href="/book/show/7029668-purge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=read-in-translation">read-in-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=world-books-challenge">world-books-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=estonia">estonia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=best-10-books-read-in-2018">best-10-books-read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2190982910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4140876177229792312">Part psychological thriller, part historical fiction, this book was not at all what I expected. You should avoid reading reviews if possible because too many give away too much, but to give a general idea, the novel begins in Estonia in 1992, where an old woman, Aliide Truu, lives alone in the countryside in an atmosphere of fear and decay. She finds a young woman, Zara, lying crumpled in her yard, and the story follows the relationship between these women and the explosive secrets they carry, t</span>
  <span id="freeText4140876177229792312" style="display:none">Part psychological thriller, part historical fiction, this book was not at all what I expected. You should avoid reading reviews if possible because too many give away too much, but to give a general idea, the novel begins in Estonia in 1992, where an old woman, Aliide Truu, lives alone in the countryside in an atmosphere of fear and decay. She finds a young woman, Zara, lying crumpled in her yard, and the story follows the relationship between these women and the explosive secrets they carry, tracing the history of Estonia back to the 1930s.<br /><br />It’s an ugly time period: from invasions by the Nazis and Russians, to decades as a repressive Soviet satellite, to lawlessness following the fall of Communism. And I wasn’t expecting the amount of horrific sexual trauma in it. It’s an intense, visceral book that draws the reader into the characters’ world, one where they don’t ever feel safe. The plot is gripping, full of secrets to be unraveled; the characters are morally complex, with believable inner worlds; the settings are vivid and the writing strong.<br /><br />Actually, my biggest complaint is not about the content, but the deckle edge pages, which publishers continue to inflict upon readers despite the fact that, if we still aren’t using e-readers, one reason is that we like to be able to easily turn pages and flip around, especially in a book like this, where readers will be inclined to re-read earlier sections in light of new information.<br /><br />I’m glad I read this book. It is an intense, compelling read, and allowed me a window into a place I knew little about, though it isn't a history book and the focus remains tightly on the experiences of the protagonists. It is dark and brutal and so isn’t for everyone, but fans of psychological thrillers will find it well worth their time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4140876177229792312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6711648016849961650">Wow. And I thought "<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2429135.The_Girl_with_the_Dragon_Tattoo__Millennium___1_' title='The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo (Millennium, #1) by Stieg Larsson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Girl with the dragon tattoo</a>" was too violent. This book takes some extreme examples of violent sexual abuse toward women and wraps a story about two women, somewhat related, around it. The authors intent here shows how little methods of control and abuse by men have changed; only the motivations have changed--as in then: political; now: profit. The horrors endured by these two have given them an uncommon common ground and their stories spin out backward from their first meeti</span>
  <span id="freeText6711648016849961650" style="display:none">Wow. And I thought "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2429135.The_Girl_with_the_Dragon_Tattoo__Millennium___1_" title="The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo (Millennium, #1) by Stieg Larsson" rel="nofollow noopener">Girl with the dragon tattoo</a>" was too violent. This book takes some extreme examples of violent sexual abuse toward women and wraps a story about two women, somewhat related, around it. The authors intent here shows how little methods of control and abuse by men have changed; only the motivations have changed--as in then: political; now: profit. The horrors endured by these two have given them an uncommon common ground and their stories spin out backward from their first meeting. Both educational and upsetting, this masterwork of fiction was an astounding feat, worthy of all the awards it has won. It is difficult for me to describe it as also a love story, but in a twisted sense, it truly is.</span>

<div id="review_1202145629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1202145629" />
    <a title="Claire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2528841-claire"><img alt="Claire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336501182p2/2528841.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1202145629?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire" href="/user/show/2528841-claire">Claire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848872134" href="/book/show/11163458-purge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2528841-claire?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2528841-claire?shelf=summer-of-women-2015">summer-of-women-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2528841-claire?shelf=around-the-world">around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2528841-claire?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2528841-claire?shelf=finnish-literature">finnish-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1202145629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5953198600079418582">Purge by Sofi Oksanen is set in a rural village in the region of Läänemaa, west Estonia. The book is translated from Finnish by Lola Rogers.<br/><br/>It is a novel of two histories, one in the late 1930's and 1940's when Aliide and her sister Ingel were adolescents, spanning the changes in their lives after Estonia was annexed by the Soviet Union and renamed Estonian Soviet Socialist Republic (ESSR) and the other in the early 1990's when a Russian-Estonian girl Zara, turns up unannounced seeking refuge.<br/><br/>At</span>
  <span id="freeText5953198600079418582" style="display:none">Purge by Sofi Oksanen is set in a rural village in the region of Läänemaa, west Estonia. The book is translated from Finnish by Lola Rogers.<br /><br />It is a novel of two histories, one in the late 1930's and 1940's when Aliide and her sister Ingel were adolescents, spanning the changes in their lives after Estonia was annexed by the Soviet Union and renamed Estonian Soviet Socialist Republic (ESSR) and the other in the early 1990's when a Russian-Estonian girl Zara, turns up unannounced seeking refuge.<br /><br />At the time of the political occupation in 1944, those who failed to do their 'political duty' of voting Estonia into the USSR were condemned to death and mass deportations occurred (half perished, the rest unable to return until the 1960's).<br /><br />The novel of five parts opens with a letter written by Hans Pekk, son of Eerik, an Estonian peasant entitled Free Estonia! Each of the five parts begins with one of his letters, which date from June 1949 until September 1951 and then the chapters alternate between 1992 (post-independence), when the dishevelled young woman Zara arrives at Aliide's home and the past, revealing Aliide's youth and the years she lived through the Soviet occupation, from 1944 until 1951.<br /><br />Zara's story flips back occasionally to 1991 in Vladivostok, Russian Federation and to Berlin the same year, before her arrival at Aliide's home. Zara is escaping brutal captors, men involved in sex slavery, human trafficking, for whom violence is an acceptable form of discipline and retribution and sex a currency of payment.<br /><br />Aliide too has her secrets, having harboured a yearning for one man for many years, an obsessive, unrequited love that lead her to make decisions and live a life of repression and lies, to trust no one and operate continuously behind a mask to protect herself and the one she loved.<br /><br />As the novel progresses and switches between era's, the stories of the two women are revealed, we move closer to learning what happened to Aliide's sister Ingel and the letter writer, Hans Pekk.<br /><br />It is a compelling read whose slow revelations fasten the pace of reading, countered by the need to pay attention to the dates, as Oksanen flips back and forth in time.<br />Against a volatile and dangerous political backdrop, the idealism, obsessive love and risk taking characteristic of youth is played out and repeated across the generations, leaving one to wonder if anything ever really changes with time. In particular, the burden, degradation and abuse of women during war and conflict and the strategies pursued by them for survival.<br /><br />Wanting to visualise where the region of Läänemaa in Estonia was, I found it was connected to a somewhat ironic slogan, “Your safe nesting place,” a reference to the areas wetlands and meadows, providing a protective habitat to its wildlife.<br /><br />It is a thought-provoking metaphor in relation to the novel, where civilians required a safe place to be protected from a different kind of predator. Is that nature? To require protection from the human predator? Is there safe refuge for those persecuted by the more brutal aspects of human power seeking? If we found ourselves living in such circumstances, how would we react?<br /><br />Purge was a bestseller in Finland, winning numerous literary prizes and has been translated into 38 languages. The Finnish-Estonian author Sofi Oksanen, was born in Finland and spent her summers in Estonia, visiting her grandmother on a kolkhoz, a Soviet collective farm, giving her an insight into a life not many outside it had access to. The story appeared as a play before the author wrote the novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5953198600079418582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17167898172526714502">You don't hear about this part of the world as often as you should. Here is one fiction writer who puts her homeland on the map with this novel of vivid imagery. A moving story of what women face during conflicts, what women faced during the Estonian conflict. <br/><br/>My problem was where the story started for me. Yes it was meant to be suspenseful but I felt teased. I think the plot could have been intertwined more with the suspense. It wasn't until I reached page 68, that I knew I wanted to keep readi</span>
  <span id="freeText17167898172526714502" style="display:none">You don't hear about this part of the world as often as you should. Here is one fiction writer who puts her homeland on the map with this novel of vivid imagery. A moving story of what women face during conflicts, what women faced during the Estonian conflict. <br /><br />My problem was where the story started for me. Yes it was meant to be suspenseful but I felt teased. I think the plot could have been intertwined more with the suspense. It wasn't until I reached page 68, that I knew I wanted to keep reading. And after Book II, well it was fast forward for me then because I was captivated. This was my first book on that part of the world so I still had unanswered questions about what was really happening there during that era, but the connection to the former Soviet Union, Siberia, and the camps, gave me some clues. The ending also left me a bit puzzled, but the connection between the two women, and the generation of abuse was devastating.</span>

<div id="review_2479914521" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2479914521" />
    <a title="Sadie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3057525-sadie"><img alt="Sadie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557910132p2/3057525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2479914521?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sadie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sadie" href="/user/show/3057525-sadie">Sadie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3057525-sadie?shelf=ty-fiction">ty-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3057525-sadie?shelf=g-novel">g-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3057525-sadie?shelf=read-author-female-only">read-author-female-only</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3057525-sadie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3057525-sadie?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3057525-sadie?shelf=z-shifting-povs">z-shifting-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3057525-sadie?shelf=medium-kindle">medium-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3057525-sadie?shelf=z-women-kicking-ass">z-women-kicking-ass</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3057525-sadie?shelf=4-stars-really-liked">4-stars-really-liked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3057525-sadie?shelf=z-shifting-timelines">z-shifting-timelines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2479914521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13179174169172601457">A dark story full of violence, betrayal, guilt and horror, set in a rather depressing place and time, written in a bleak way - no, this isn't any kind of happy-go-lucky-story. However, reading this was most satisfying, since as a dark novel, as a work of literary fiction that makes one fret, it delivers on all accounts.<br/><br/>It's a story of two women, seperated by many years and lots of history, united in their fate largely shaped by men (and their own reactions towards what these men do - or didn't d</span>
  <span id="freeText13179174169172601457" style="display:none">A dark story full of violence, betrayal, guilt and horror, set in a rather depressing place and time, written in a bleak way - no, this isn't any kind of happy-go-lucky-story. However, reading this was most satisfying, since as a dark novel, as a work of literary fiction that makes one fret, it delivers on all accounts.<br /><br />It's a story of two women, seperated by many years and lots of history, united in their fate largely shaped by men (and their own reactions towards what these men do - or didn't do). Aliide is the older of the two and more like the main character. Her actions determine pretty much the whole outcome of the novel. She isn't a really sympathetic character, despite the things she has to go through and that hardened her. We get to know her fate step by step, the novel switches back and forth in time and gradually peels away the layers of unrequited love, political opression, the decline of a family and lots and lots of violence. <br /><br />The younger woman, Zara, is, in some way, the result of those years of love/hate, betrayal and deceipt - at the same time, her own fate was shaped in a similarly violent way. Both women, each in their own respective way, did everything they could for their dream to come true - only to find their dream not just shattered, but exploding right in front of their face. <br /><br />Make no mistake, this is a tough read, and even though it's spiced with a pinch of redemption every now and then, the impact of "OMG, how could you" keeps the upper hand. And it all fits, the darkness, the bleak tone, the - for me - rather exotic setting of (politically) surpressed Estonia. For this is not only a story about two women, but also about a country, a time &amp; place, about the Estonian people trying to find their way.<br /><br />Spoiler for the ending - don't peak if you consider reading this at some point, it's for your own good, trust me... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kudos to Sofi Oksanen for the final twist revealed in the "Top Secret Files". Just as I was getting ready to grant Aliide <i>some</i> idea of redemption - even after what she did to Hans, in the end, she kind of "came full circle" by killing Zara's pimps - the secret files revealed her spying and ultimate very own responsibility for her sister's deportation, and I really didn't see that coming. What a blow, what a final shocking twist. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Absolutely recommended for those who like their reading material to take them one step further into the dark unknown.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13179174169172601457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_104236503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104236503" />
    <a title=" ManOfLaBook.com" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3780991-manoflabook-com"><img alt=" ManOfLaBook.com" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294067272p2/3780991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104236503?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" ManOfLaBook.com" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" ManOfLaBook.com" href="/user/show/3780991-manoflabook-com"> ManOfLaBook.com</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780802170774" href="/book/show/7029668-purge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3780991-manoflabook-com?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104236503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2389364408575287279">This book tells the story of three generations of Estonian women (and the men in their lives). The book chapters jump in time to tell the tale of some horrifying events in their lives which correspond to the historical events which take Estonia, in general, and their rural village specifically through WWII, soviet rule and independence. <br/><br/>The story centers around two women, Aliide Truu and Zara who is the victim of a sex-trafficking operation and ends up in Aliide's home while running away from he</span>
  <span id="freeText2389364408575287279" style="display:none">This book tells the story of three generations of Estonian women (and the men in their lives). The book chapters jump in time to tell the tale of some horrifying events in their lives which correspond to the historical events which take Estonia, in general, and their rural village specifically through WWII, soviet rule and independence. <br /><br />The story centers around two women, Aliide Truu and Zara who is the victim of a sex-trafficking operation and ends up in Aliide's home while running away from her captors. Only that Zara has a picture of Aliide and her sister, her arrival wasn't coincidental. <br /><br />There is a psychological side to this book, which I felt was more fascinating than the historical side. Aliide's motivations are a product of lost love and jealously, but her actions are a product of survival in an oppressing society; she cheats on her husband and turns in her sister to the authorities. Hans, Aliide's brother in law and the subject of her fantasies, is a Nazi sympathizer and a murderer. Zara goes looking for easy money and gets caught up in the harsh and violent world of prostitution. When Zara arrives on Aliide's doorstep, a Pandora's box is opened and shines a light of decades of abused women both in Communistic as well as Democratic societies. <br /><br />As mentioned, the book is not written in chronological order, but the story unfolds very simply, in a country where nothing seems as it is, under a government which is vigilant, oppressive, cruel and paranoid, yet has taken the role of a nanny which has many people so dependent on it they almost forgot how to take care of themselves. <br /><br />The characters in this book are drawn very well, no-one is what he or she seems to be, the world is filled with dangers and the extremes we (Americans) are so used to simple do not exist. <br /><br />The women in this novel purge their soul, name and their past. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2389364408575287279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=2016-books">2016-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1668305786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7381066279209488447"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466234365i/19454991._SX540_.jpg' width='320' height='240' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Estonian forest.<br/><br/>Wow! What a story!<br/><br/>If it weren't for my book club, I wouldn't have picked this book up! I tried reading this 4 years ago, but due to a hectic schedule, ultimately gave up. However, four days ago, I picked it up again and was sucked into the story!<br/><br/>Where do I begin? One morning in 1992, Aliide Truu, an elderly woman, who used to be a Communist when Estonia was part of the Soviet Union, finds a bruised young woman in her garden. Now if I were Aliide, I would have rushed outside to he</span>
  <span id="freeText7381066279209488447" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466234365i/19454991._SX540_.jpg" width="320" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Estonian forest.<br><br>Wow! What a story!<br><br>If it weren't for my book club, I wouldn't have picked this book up! I tried reading this 4 years ago, but due to a hectic schedule, ultimately gave up. However, four days ago, I picked it up again and was sucked into the story!<br><br>Where do I begin? One morning in 1992, Aliide Truu, an elderly woman, who used to be a Communist when Estonia was part of the Soviet Union, finds a bruised young woman in her garden. Now if I were Aliide, I would have rushed outside to help the girl and call help. However, Aliide approaches the situation with a very high level of distrust and believes the girl is a decoy. <br><br><i>Purge</i> gives the reader a good general overview of Estonia from when the country was occupied by Soviets and Germans during World War II to its relapse to Soviet communist rule for the next fifty years. The book traces where Aliide Truu's mistrust comes from. I now also understand why Estonia has close ties to Germany and have learned that Estonians are closely related to Finnish people (both Estonian and Finnish are Uralic languages, not Indo-European). <br><br>The author skips a lot between the past and the present, and different narrators are used at random. Themes, which are dealt intensively in this book includes; horrendous prostitution, human trafficking and the Russian mafia, sibling rivalry, obsessive love, betrayal, self-reliance, and how the communist system turned people against each other. There are some truly gruesome scenes in this book, so it's not a light read, but definitely a page-turner!<br><br>Overall, this book gave me a real taste of this Eastern European country, its Communist past and how a shadow of the past still lingers around in the present. </span>

<div id="review_113610412" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113610412" />
    <a title="Elizabeth (Alaska)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2026178-elizabeth-alaska"><img alt="Elizabeth (Alaska)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304966095p2/2026178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113610412?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth (Alaska)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth (Alaska)" href="/user/show/2026178-elizabeth-alaska">Elizabeth (Alaska)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848872110" href="/book/show/7980827-purge">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=twenty-first-century">twenty-first-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=europe-other">europe-other</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=women">women</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113610412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7892020703916139250">My thoughts are all over the place. I think if I had not first read her <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22318383.When_the_Doves_Disappeared' title='When the Doves Disappeared by Sofi Oksanen' rel='nofollow noopener'>When the Doves Disappeared</a>, I might not have had any understanding of what happened to Estonia in WWII. It was invaded by the Soviets, then "rescued" by the Germans, only to return to Soviet rule before war's end. There is only a passing mention of German occupation in this, instead focusing on the tyranny and brutality of the Soviets. <br/><br/>I hereby emphasize the brutality. This book is not for the squeamish nor faint-of-heart. T</span>
  <span id="freeText7892020703916139250" style="display:none">My thoughts are all over the place. I think if I had not first read her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22318383.When_the_Doves_Disappeared" title="When the Doves Disappeared by Sofi Oksanen" rel="nofollow noopener">When the Doves Disappeared</a>, I might not have had any understanding of what happened to Estonia in WWII. It was invaded by the Soviets, then "rescued" by the Germans, only to return to Soviet rule before war's end. There is only a passing mention of German occupation in this, instead focusing on the tyranny and brutality of the Soviets. <br /><br />I hereby emphasize the brutality. This book is not for the squeamish nor faint-of-heart. There is not a rape scene, but there can be no mistake that it happened. There are other scenes of abuse, some of which are quite graphic. I think there are no good men in this novel. Aliide's husband, Martin, is sort of neutral, but he is a party member and a communist, and is only tolerated. Aliide has a sister, Ingel, who married Hans Pekk. Hans is wanted for fighting as an anti-Soviet, but his page time is for other reasons and I was unable to warm to him.<br /><br />At one point I questioned why I read novels that contain such violence against women. Away from the book, I realized it's because nonfiction can't do what fiction can. Although nonfiction can tell us about brutality, there is a lack of emotion. With fiction, we have someone with whom we can sympathize and what happens becomes real. I think it is important to fully understand what can happen (and has happened) when the people give government too much power. <br /><br />There is a story, of course. In the opening it is 1992, Läänemaa, Estonia. Aliide Truu finds Zara in her yard. Why is she there, what does she want? Can Zara be trusted? Is she a decoy for thieves? As for Zara, must she hide the truth? The chapters are dated with locations. Nearly all are in Läänemaa, but because of dates much of it is in the Estonian Soviet Socialist Republic. Some small amount takes place in Vladivostok, Russian Federation and Berlin, Germany. The timeline is not linear, but reading the chapter headings eliminates all confusion. The ending requires careful reading, something I might have skimped on. <br /><br />I must remark on Oksanen's prose, because it is this which gives flesh to the novel. She manages to write sentences and paragraphs that in their very structure create tension. It isn't just in <i>what</i> she says, but in <i>how</i> she says it. I would say also that, while the characterizations might be less than I could hope for, we fully understand the motivations of the two women who are the main characters. No one could misunderstand the very smell of fear and distrust. <br /><br />This was another 5-star read for me. I could not take a steady diet of Sofi Oksanen, but neither do I want to forget her. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7892020703916139250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_106035028" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106035028" />
    <a title="Milka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1982249-milka"><img alt="Milka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514931022p2/1982249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106035028?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Milka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Milka" href="/user/show/1982249-milka">Milka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1982249-milka?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1982249-milka?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106035028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3166722361446532555">Wow. For the first time in a long time I can honestly say that I am proud about being Finnish and proud about the fact that I speak language such as Finnish as my mother tongue.<br/><br/> <br/><br/>After winning the Finlandia Prize (the most prestigious literary award in Finland, awarded to the best fiction book, best children's book and best non-fiction book, 30,000 euros) Sofi Oksanen has been everywhere. Literally. She is in the news, in the newspapers, everywhere. Probably a week after she won the prize I got t</span>
  <span id="freeText3166722361446532555" style="display:none">Wow. For the first time in a long time I can honestly say that I am proud about being Finnish and proud about the fact that I speak language such as Finnish as my mother tongue.<br /><br /> <br /><br />After winning the Finlandia Prize (the most prestigious literary award in Finland, awarded to the best fiction book, best children's book and best non-fiction book, 30,000 euros) Sofi Oksanen has been everywhere. Literally. She is in the news, in the newspapers, everywhere. Probably a week after she won the prize I got totally annoyed of her and her praised novel, Purge (Puhdistus). I did not know what the novel was about, and I did not even want to know.<br /><br /> <br /><br />Like you can probably guess from my previous paragraph, I had a huge amount of negative expectations towards this novel. I visit the bookstores weekly and every week this novel has been on the "most sold" shelf. Now when I broke my ankle and I am just spending time at home, I told my mother to bring me it from the library. I was too curious to pass it.<br /><br /><br />I am so happy that I overlooked my negative taughts and read this book. All the way from the beginning of the book I knew that I would like it. The way Oksanen uses the Finnish language (yes, I read this in Finnish, which is really rare, since I mostly read in English) is amazing. I did not even know you can use it like that without making it hard to understand. I would love if you would have a change to read this in Finnish too, but probably the translation is pretty good as well. I saw the English copy of this novel at the local bookstore, maybe I buy it at some point and read it since this is definitely one of those books I will want to go back to.<br /><br /> <br /><br />The Purge tells a story through the eyes and thoughts of three different characters. Aliide Truu is a elderly woman living alone in the Estonian coutryside. One day she notices a body of a girl laying on her yard. The girl, Zara, is in need of help. She has left from her home to the West, to Germany, in hope of a money for studying. The work that was promised to her turned out to be something very different she thought, and she notices that she is working as a prostitute for an employee who is ready to do anything to keep her working. Aliide decides decides to help her and by seeing a photo Zara carries around she discovers that it is not by coincidence that Zara popped out to her yard. <br /><br /><br />As the story develops, the past of both characters, Aliide and Zara, is opened to the reader. Aliide's youth, her love to her sister's husband Hans and the acts she was ready to do in order make him love her are described wividly. Zara's past is told as it is, violent and disturbing. What I really liked about this was the fact that the sexual abuse Zara experienced was told without hesitation. It really opened my eyes about the situation Zara was in. The novel also introduces us to Hans, who through his journal entries opens up his story. I think that the journal entries were a great addition to this novel since otherwise the story is about the situation of women. By reading the journal entries by Hans we get to know what was going on in a man's head.<br /><br /> <br /><br />The disturbing harshes of the lifes of these two women, the despair of Hans in losing this wife and daughter, the passionate love of Aliide towards Hans and Zara's hope of better future make this story a breathtaking read. It opens up the Estonian history by introducing us to there three very different personalities who have a deep connection between them.<br /><br /> <br /><br />It is hard to define how wonderful this book was by using words. You just have to read it by yourself. I cannot believe I am actually saying this about a Finnish book. I think this is actually the first Finnish novel I ever review to my blog. So that shows you how much Finnish literature I read. I am so happy this book will be published on different languages, since I want others to have a change to read this amazing novel about passionate love, despair, shame, history, the need for home and the want to be free. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3166722361446532555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WLwb2jmbOn+SB31rZY1Tf23dWblrZarMlRao+DMvqFrXZ6p3K2c/AwqqsBadS00gtQx4K4GxPUZYoIij/OvUOg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aH7aCf8VptsNapL8xreggaSCxkYLOnPSxmUc9BObLCXnpWuk7emjp5XHX4E+cb7efFPn1OHu5FgL0zyv3F9QRQ==')})
  }

The crowning accomplishment of Finland\'s first literary genius, Seven Brothers remains &quot;the greatest Finnish novel of all time&quot;, the classic among the classics in Finnish literature. Published in 1870, in the author\'s 36th year and two years before his untimely death, Seven Brothers laid the foundation for what Kai Laitinen later called &quot;The Great Tradition in Finnish Prose&quot;. This tradition is characterized by realism, humor, respect for the common people, and depiction of nature as both friend and foe. Received at the time of publication by uncomprehending arbiters of literary taste, who still delighted in romantic approaches to literature, Seven Brothers fared poorly in early reviews. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13741832068395687412">Sofi Oksanen was born in Finland to a Finnish father and an Estonian mother. In 2010 she won the Nordic Council's Literature Prize for her third novel (originally a play), <i>Puhdistus</i> (<i>Purge</i>).</span>
